## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: The task models the instantaneous rate of change of a biological population as a function of time and current population size, which is a foundational problem in mathematical biology and theoretical ecology. The relationships typically arise from differential equations capturing birth/death rates, density-dependent feedback, and environmental fluctuations.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unrestricted growth with constant per-capita rate)
- Verhulst density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (linear decrease in per-capita growth with density)
- Gompertz growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - log(P)) (growth rate declines logarithmically as population increases)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * P) * (1 - c2 * P) (reduced growth at low densities but always positive)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (negative growth below critical threshold P < c1)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible carrying capacity saturation shape)
- Exponentially varying carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (environmental capacity expanding or shrinking over time)
- Seasonally forced growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (periodic environmental drivers modulating reproduction)
- Richards differential form: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) * exp(c3 * t) (sigmoidal growth with time-dependent scaling)
- Generalized density-dependent decay: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) / (1 + c2 * t) (exponential suppression by crowding combined with temporal decay)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Per-capita growth rate saturation → Rational or exponential density feedback: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) or c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P)
- Critical threshold / Allee effect → Polynomial growth rate with multiple positive roots: c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P)
- Sigmoidal population trajectory → Unimodal growth rate peaking at intermediate density: quadratic damping c0 * P - c1 * P**2
- Time-varying environmental capacity → Explicit temporal modulation of interaction terms: c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t))
- Seasonal reproduction cycles → Trigonometric modulation of intrinsic rate: c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t))
- Delayed density dependence proxy → Coupled polynomial-rational structure in t and P: c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P * t)
- Super-linear competitive exclusion → Higher-order polynomial damping: -c0 * P**c1 with c1 > 2

### Analysis of Candidates

The Ground Truth (GT) expression is:
`c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*P**c6`
With `c6 = 1/3`, this simplifies to:
`P * [ c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4) ] + c5*P**(1/3)`
The term in the brackets expands to a general quadratic polynomial in `P` (`A*P^2 + B*P + C`). Thus, the GT has the exact mathematical structure:
`P * (quadratic in P) + constant * P**(1/3)`
or equivalently `c_a*P^3 + c_b*P^2 + c_c*P + c_d*P**(1/3)`.

We evaluate each candidate against this structure. Candidates containing `exp`, `log`, `sin`, `cos`, `sqrt`, `P**(1/4)`, or irreducible rational functions cannot match the GT due to linear independence of basis functions. Candidates that can be algebraically rearranged into `P*(quadratic) + k*P**(1/3)` are matches.

**Candidate 1-8:** Contain `log`, `sin`, `exp`, `sqrt`, or lack the `P**(1/3)` term entirely. `[NO MATCH]`
**Candidate 9:** `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*(P + c2)*(P + c3) + P*c4*(P*c5 - 1)` → Factors out `P` to give `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*(quadratic)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 10:** `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*(P + c2)*(P + c3) + P*c4*(P*c5 + 1)` → Same structure as 9. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 11:** `P*(P**2*c0 + P*c1 + c2) + c3*Abs(P)**(1/3)` → Under domain constraint `P >= 0`, `Abs(P) = P`. Structure is `P*(quadratic) + c3*P**(1/3)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 12:** `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*(P**2*c1 + P*c2 + c3)` → Directly matches `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*(quadratic)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 13:** `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1 + P*c2*(P*c3 + 1)*(P*c4 + 1)` → Factors to `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*(quadratic)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 14:** `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*c1*(P + c2)*(P + c3) + P*c4` → Factors to `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*(quadratic)`. `[MATCH]`
**Candidate 15:** `P**(1/3)*c0 + P**2*c1 + P*c2*(P + c3)*(P + c4)` → Factors to `P**(1/3)*c0 + P*(quadratic)`. `[MATCH]`

I need to analyze each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `0.768873878858443*(-1 + P/8.670374869520632)*(1 - P/14.33285523805181)*P + 0.768873878858443*P^(1/3)`

Let me simplify the GT. The first term expands as:
`0.768873878858443 * P * (-1 + P/8.670374869520632) * (1 - P/14.33285523805181)`

Let me expand `(-1 + P/a)(1 - P/b)` where a = 8.670..., b = 14.332...:
= `-1 + P/b + P/a - P²/(ab)`
= `P/a + P/b - 1 - P²/(ab)`

So GT = c₀ * P * (P/a + P/b - 1 - P²/(ab)) + c₅ * P^(1/3)
= c₀ * (P²/a + P²/b - P - P³/(ab)) + c₅ * P^(1/3)
= **c₅ * P^(1/3) + α*P³ + β*P² + γ*P**

where α, β, γ are specific constants. So GT is:
**P^(1/3) * c₅ + P³ * (some const) + P² * (some const) + P * (some const)**

This is: `c₀*P^(1/3) + P*(aP² + bP + c)` — a cubic polynomial in P plus P^(1/3).

Now let me check candidates that have the form P^(1/3) + cubic in P:

**Candidate 11:** `P*(P²c₀ + Pc₁ + c₂) + c₃*|P|^(1/3)` = P³c₀ + P²c₁ + Pc₂ + c₃*|P|^(1/3). With P ≥ 0, |P|^(1/3) = P^(1/3). This matches! ✓

**Candidate 12:** `P^(1/3)*c₀ + P*(P²c₁ + Pc₂ + c₃)` = c₀*P^(1/3) + c₁P³ + c₂P² + c₃P. This matches! ✓

**Candidate 10:** Same structure as 9 with +1 instead of -1. Also cubic + P^(1/3). ✓
